<div id="review_1647791187" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1647791187" />
    <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell"><img alt="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584062476p2/2190064.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1647791187?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell">Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=ya-ya-land">ya-ya-land</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=best-young-adult-books">best-young-adult-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1647791187" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9499406845706017951"><a href='http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/alwaysbeebooked/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/>Confession: when this book first came out with the original cover, I thought it was a book about ballet.<br/><br/><br/><br/>Spoiler alert: this book is not about ballet.<br/><br/><br/><br/>When a new young adult title gets released, two things inevitably happen:<br/><br/>1) a whole swarm of bloggers read the book, talk about <i>how they can't even, you guys!</i>, and rate it five stars.<br/><br/>2) <i>I </i>read the book in question, wonder if I'm in a parallel universe where good books turn into bad books, an</span>
  <span id="freeText9499406845706017951" style="display:none"><a href="http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/alwaysbeebooked/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br>Confession: when this book first came out with the original cover, I thought it was a book about ballet.<br><br><br><br>Spoiler alert: this book is not about ballet.<br><br><br><br>When a new young adult title gets released, two things inevitably happen:<br><br>1) a whole swarm of bloggers read the book, talk about <i>how they can't even, you guys!</i>, and rate it five stars.<br><br>2) <i>I </i>read the book in question, wonder if I'm in a parallel universe where good books turn into bad books, and rate the book one or two stars.<br><br><br><br>With THE WINNER'S CURSE, I suffered no reader's remorse. This is pretty much everything I expect from young adult - it deals real issues in an intelligent and sophisticated way without talking down to the audience at all. The heroine is calculating, clever, brilliant- a military strategist who is a champion at her world's equivalent of chess. The hero is dark and dangerous, but not in a contrived way. His backstory is quite sad and heart-wrenching, and he has depth to his behavior that makes him seem less scary and more like an honest-to-god love interest.<br><br><br><br>THE WINNER'S CURSE is about two societies: the Valorians and the Herrani. The Valorians are fair, militaristic, and obsessed with honor. The Herrani, on the other hand, are artisans and intellectuals, who put a premium on artistry and religion, although they also had a powerful navy. The Valorians were jealous of all that the Herrani had achieved - and so, the Valorians decided to take it, and enslave the very people that they had once held in admiration, reducing them to the status of animals as they took them all as their slaves in the very villas where they once resided.<br><br><br><br>Kestrel is the daughter of a powerful general in the Valorian army. One day, while in the marketplace with her friend, Jess, she comes to a slave auction by accident. She sees a young, attractive man whose rebellious streak will doom him to a life of beatings. Out of a misguided sense of something, she purchases him - and the decision ends up changing her life in unexpected ways. The slave, Arin, is not all that he seems...and as her relationship to him grows closer, it could mean her doom.<br><br><br><br>Who doesn't love doom in their romances?<br><br><br><br>One of the best things about THE WINNER'S CURSE was the complexity of the characters. They are both very suspicious, clever people who are good at getting into the heads of others. Watching them try to read each other and gauge one another's thoughts was like watching a chess match between two skilled chess players. This was really well done, and it was especially refreshing to see a female main character who could keep the male main character on his toes, and even best him on occasion.<br><br><br><br>Boy, this book ended on the mother of all cliffhangers, though. It seems to be going THE HUNGER GAMES route, and I think I can espy a love triangle on the horizon. Honestly, though - at this point, I'm game. Rutkoski has proved herself worthy. THE WINNER'S CURSE is that rare book in a hundred that actually lives up to the hype.<br><br><br><br>4.5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9499406845706017951" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1909309688" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1909309688?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin">Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

  <span id="freeText1162035293197694336" style="display:none">That ending! What are Kestrel and Arin going to do now? These poor people had to live as slaves in their own town and even in some of their own homes. RUDE! <br><br>Anyway, Kestrel was out gambling one day (she's pretty good at it) and her and her best friend, Jess end up at the slave market. Kestrel ends up buying a slave because of reasons and a lot of it was a set up for, reasons. &lt;--- I love saying that in my book reviews. <br><br>Arin is an amazing blacksmith and he's working or Kestrel's household and there is something brewing there. Arin and Kestrel become friends, slowly but surely. <br><br>Kestrel plays the piano beautifully. BUT, her father wants her to go into the military. They have a rule that Valorians have to get married or join the military by age 21. RUDE! I mean good grief, these people don't have the lives they want, even though they are jerks for making slaves and killing people. <br><br>Then other things happen and there is a big war brewing, plots being made, etc . . . .<br><br>I loved Kestrel, Arin, Jess and Enai. ♥<br><br>Kestrel wasn't a bad@ass, she even admitted she couldn't fight even though her father had her taking lessons for years. She just wanted to play her music and be left alone. But she was very smart and asked her father to let her started talking strategies and politics with him. If she's not bad@ssed on the fighting ground at least she has a brain to think up things better than these men. &lt;-- Sorry boys. <br><br>Anyhoo, all of this helps her in the end but uggggggg, why? <div id="review_1283761623" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1283761623" />
    <a title="Jasmine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21803154-jasmine"><img alt="Jasmine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582366251p2/21803154.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1283761623?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasmine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasmine" href="/user/show/21803154-jasmine">Jasmine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">EVERYONE!!!!!</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jasmine by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/24842656-lisa">Lisa</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=beautiful-stories">beautiful-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=cliffhanger">cliffhanger</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=ebooks-ibooks">ebooks-ibooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=great-fighting-scenes">great-fighting-scenes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=highly-recommend">highly-recommend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=will-reread">will-reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=strong-emotions">strong-emotions</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=deja-vu">deja-vu</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1283761623" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10629842945857432089"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Kestrel thought about how this might be what hurt the most.<br/>That they had used something she loved against her."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Maybe I shouldn't judge someone or something by my first impression on them, but I can't help myself. So it's official that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1238111.Marie_Rutkoski' title='Marie Rutkoski' rel='nofollow noopener'>Marie Rutkoski</a> becomes one of my top favorite authors and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16069030.The_Winner_s_Curse__The_Winner_s_Trilogy___1_' title='The Winner's Curse (The Winner's Trilogy, #1) by Marie Rutkoski' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Winner's Curse</a> my top favorite books of all time. I can't stop admiring how wonderful her writing style and how incredibly well-written this story is. She tells the story in a pretty easy ye</span>
  <span id="freeText10629842945857432089" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Kestrel thought about how this might be what hurt the most.<br>That they had used something she loved against her."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Maybe I shouldn't judge someone or something by my first impression on them, but I can't help myself. So it's official that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1238111.Marie_Rutkoski" title="Marie Rutkoski" rel="nofollow noopener">Marie Rutkoski</a> becomes one of my top favorite authors and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16069030.The_Winner_s_Curse__The_Winner_s_Trilogy___1_" title="The Winner's Curse (The Winner's Trilogy, #1) by Marie Rutkoski" rel="nofollow noopener">The Winner's Curse</a> my top favorite books of all time. I can't stop admiring how wonderful her writing style and how incredibly well-written this story is. She tells the story in a pretty easy yet powerful way--<b>short, concise descriptions, no redundant narrations, and every conversation among the characters is simple and clear</b>--she doesn't beat around the bush and what impresses me most is that she still manages to make us emotional.<br><br><b>Kestrel</b> is an ultra-clever girl with a small frame. <b>She’s an impressive strategist</b> and wins her battles with her brain instead of the physical strength. She knows how to use a secret or scandal against her opponents and at the same time, stealthily creeps into others' minds so that they’ll believe what she wants them to believe. Then, the people will easily become pieces in the game she's determined to win in the end.<br><br><b>Arin</b> is a slave who defies orders and dares to stare into Kestrel's eyes head on with his own beautiful grey ones. He's contemplating his next move all the time and so is she. He's setting different tiles at <a href="http://thewinnerstrilogy.com/bite-sting.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Bite and Sting</a> and she, too, is willing to play the game until the end. <br><br><b>
  <u>I know she's going to purchase him at a much higher price at the auction. What I don't know is that it happens so quickly in the beginning.</u>
</b><br><blockquote>
  <i>Then she reminded herself bitterly that this was what curiosity had bought her: fifty keystones for a singer who refused to sing, a friend who wasn’t her friend, someone who was hers and yet would never be hers.</i>
</blockquote><br><b>
  <u>I know she's going to have feelings for him but it'll break her heart eventually. What I don't know is that the disappointment is so strong that when it hits me, my heart aches badly.</u>
</b><br><blockquote>
  <i>Why didn’t he come to her?<br>She could make him. If she sent an order, he would obey.<br>But she didn’t want his obedience. She wanted him to want to see her.<br>Kestrel flinched at this thought and the pain it brought with it.<br>She knew that even if everyone believed the wrong thing of her, they were also too close to being right.</i>
</blockquote><br><b>
  <u>I also know that she will never be his friend. What I don't know is that he will change his mind.</u>
</b><br><blockquote>
  <i>“You might not think of me as your friend,” Kestrel told Arin, “but I think of you as mine.”<br>...<br>“But am I your enemy?” Arin crossed the space between them. Softly, he repeated, “Am I?”<br>…<br>“You’re not mine,” Arin said.</i>
</blockquote><br><i>The Winner's Curse</i> overwhelms me with its never-ending brilliance and vigor, and all the fascinating plans carefully calculated by those characters. Although the story itself reminds me of many other YA stories, there's nothing entirely similar in particular that I can point out. That's another thumbs-up for this trilogy. <br><br>One last thing I really, really love about the book is that <b>neither Kestrel nor Arin is avoiding each other or pushing the other away.</b> I mean, <s>lots of dystopian romances have the pattern of main character A pushes main character B away throughout the book and B finds something special in A later and then A forgives B and they live happily ever after.</s> It's so NOT the case in this book! <br><br><b>The romance is slow-paced because both of them are baiting their own traps and play their own games.</b> I feel like entering their mind game when I read the first chapter and they leave me with a heart-wrenching cliffhanger. <b>The biggest difference is that Kestrel and Arin talk.</b> They communicate and share their thoughts despite the fact that one is the captor and the other prisoner. Regardlessly, <b>a part of them work together as a team, whereas a part of them secretly plot out the rest to make the other pay.</b> All in all, their interaction is the most precious thing in this novel and I cherish those moments wholeheartedly. <br><blockquote>
  <i>“Open your hands, Little Fists,” said Arin. “Open your eyes. I haven’t stolen his love for you. Look.” It was true that in the course of their conversation, Javelin had turned away from Arin, disappointed by the empty pocket. The horse nosed Kestrel’s shoulder. “See?” Arin said. “He knows the difference between an easy mark and his mistress.”</i>
</blockquote><br>Lastly, here's a playlist I think it fits the atmosphere in this story so much.<br>1)<a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2i2khp_npdE" rel="nofollow noopener">Alan Walker-Sing Me To Sleep</a><br>"Wait a second let me catch my breath<br>Remind me of how it feels to hear your voice<br>Your lips are moving; I can't hear a thing<br>Living life as if we had a choice<br>Anywhere, anytime, I will do anything for you"<br><br>2)<a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=CPik5voZ96I" rel="nofollow noopener">Natasha Thomas-Let Me Show You The Way</a><br>"Are you gonna be there when I need someone<br> And will I be always just the only one<br> I don't wanna have just another heartbreak<br> So tell me is your love true or a fake in the game of the heart<br> You know I know that you are mine"<br><br>3)<a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=xLPGtQoRUbk" rel="nofollow noopener">Kodaline-The One</a><br>"When we are together you make me feel like my mind is free<br> And my dreams are reachable<br> You know I never ever believed in love or believed one day<br> That you would come along"<br><br>To sum up, I love this book very much so I <b>HIGHLY RECOMMEND</b> it to everyone!<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1467188101i/19561496._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="10629842945857432089" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_878405028" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/878405028" />
    <a title="Mitch" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8170554-mitch"><img alt="Mitch" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396208595p2/8170554.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/878405028?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mitch" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mitch" href="/user/show/8170554-mitch">Mitch</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8170554-mitch?shelf=no-just-no">no-just-no</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer878405028" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8539155909255977865"><b>Why do I feel like I just read something out of the Spartacus fanfiction reject pile?</b><br/><br/>To be perfectly honest, I thought I'd seen the very bottom of bad young adult historical fantasy. Not gonna name names, but even among such esteemed company, <u>The Winner's Curse</u> is a new low. However you want to measure it, plot, setting, character development, Marie Rutkoski's latest book fundamentally fails at being anything other than bland, shallow, cliched, and predictable. Maybe I'm being spoiled by fond me</span>
  <span id="freeText8539155909255977865" style="display:none"><b>Why do I feel like I just read something out of the Spartacus fanfiction reject pile?</b><br /><br />To be perfectly honest, I thought I'd seen the very bottom of bad young adult historical fantasy. Not gonna name names, but even among such esteemed company, <u>The Winner's Curse</u> is a new low. However you want to measure it, plot, setting, character development, Marie Rutkoski's latest book fundamentally fails at being anything other than bland, shallow, cliched, and predictable. Maybe I'm being spoiled by fond memories of Melina Marchetta, Kristin Cashore, and Maria V. Snyder, but I really expected more from this book, and all I got out of it was the biting anticipation of finishing a train wreck I just couldn't look away from. <br /><br />I'm surprised no one has mentioned this yet, but my first reaction? - what a <b>a blatant knockoff of Spartacus</b>, and not a good one at that. You have your <s>Roman</s> er Valorian Empire and all the backstory predictably associated with that. You have your supposedly charismatic slave leader Arin (never mind he has the personality of a dull block of wood) who not surprisingly is revealed to be a ringleader of a planned slave rebellion not too many chapters in. The rest, as anyone who's seen one of the many incarnations of Spartacus can attest to (I'm partial to the Starz version myself), is much murder, mayhem, violence, and killing of <s>Romans</s> Valorians, only in this case, everything's sanitized and not much of it makes any sense (I'll get back to that in a moment). Unfortunately, while Rutkoski borrows just enough of Roman culture, history, and trappings to make it obvious, the lore, mythos, world building, whatever you want to call it, behind this world is bad, like really bad. The setting's not really well developed, with enough name dropping (congratulations Dacians, you're now the Dacrans!) that we're not dealing with a blank canvas here but beyond that there's no richness or flavor that makes me go, hmm, Rutkoski really gets the Romans (see, e.g., anything by Elizabeth Bear for comparison's sake). Normally, that's not a fatal flaw, but in this case, we have slaves who I would literally forget were slaves based on their behavior and how they're treated if Rutkoski hadn't kept reminding me (I'm not saying an author has to go all in like Steve McQueen in <u>12 Years a Slave</u>, but when slavery is such a crucial part of your book, it's borderline insulting to both your audience and history to portray them like well off servants for the most part) and a second half that relies so much on political intrigue that it completely fails at making sense because Rutkoski doesn't take the time to explain the why, especially given how contrary it is to everything that's happened in the preceding chapters (the last few chapters were complete WTFs to me). <br /><br />Which leads me to my next complaint - the real problem isn't the boring, borrowed, shallow backstory, it's that <b>none of the characters behave in character</b> (actually, I'm being pretty generous calling these cardboard cutouts 'characters' and assuming they're intended to have a character, but I probably shouldn't go there). Kestrel, for example, is written both as a vapid society girl and a supposed military genius, and now I'm not saying a kickass heroine can't also be a little vain, but her two halves do not gel. She's supposed to be torn by her feeling for Arin and her loyalties to the Valorians, but if so, Rutkoski does a poor job of it, because all I see is a lovestruck girl who doesn't give two shits about her country except as an obligatory aside, and all that does is make me question every choice she ends up making - like, why does she do this? How does that make any sense? And it goes without saying she, heck the entire book, would've been much more interesting had Rutkoski developed Kestrel as the kind of character who's uncomfortable living in a slaveholding society despite that world being the only one she knows, but that part of the book is so glossed over there's no tension there and makes the eventual role reversal when Arin's rebellion breaks out all the more ridiculous. And that's not even mentioning the complete fail of all the supporting characters - young adult as a genre is usually good at delivering the best (girl) friend, the best (guy) friend, and the jackass suitor tropes, but these? You're kidding, right? Critically, this is a book without real villains, the whole premise relies on the shades of gray of humans, Valorians, accepting the inhumanity of slavery and the consequences of that acceptance when the slaves overthrow their masters, but such a book really needs exceptional, nuanced characters to work and none of Rutkoski's stepped up to the plate and made me want to care about what was going on.<br /><br />So what's left? A plot that left me wondering, is everyone in this book really that dumb? Seriously, I don't know how else to explain Arin plotting rebellion under everyone's noses and nobody, including Kestrel who's supposed to be incredibly perceptive, noticing anything. I guess given all the other fail, asking for a clandestine, suspenseful conspiracy is a little too much, but this is the worst kind of handholding where everything that happens is viewed through the lens of (and supposed to fuel) the growing angst of these two star-crossed lovers. Eh. Otherwise, there's no twists, no turns, no complex characters, no exploration of a relationship between a girl and the slave she bought besides the tritest of batting eyelashes, and no resolutions except those that are clearly of the 'because the author said so' variety; it's all meaningless pining, generic action sequences, some nonsense leading to the kind of ending I can't explain except to say, gee, how does this even work except to make the sequel even more angsty and gut wrenching? - I could go on and on about how the actual story feels like a hollow, dumbed down shell of a premise, a complete letdown of what I thought the teasers promised, but like I said, after the first five chapters I was steeling myself for the train wreck to come and yet despite my morbid curiosity and sense of schadenfreude keeping me going I was still unprepared for how unexpectedly devoid of emotion, genuinely awful, and completely tangential to the premise this thing degenerates into.<br /><br /><br />Frankly, I'm not exactly sure what the appeal of this book is. In terms of borrowing from Roman history and culture, in terms of building characters separated by slavery, in terms of delivering a plot that logically goes from point A to point B without devolving into a hot mess, <u>The Winner's Curse</u> completely misses the mark on all fronts.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8539155909255977865" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review878405028">

<div id="review_1575587444" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1575587444" />
    <a title="Beth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44125660-beth"><img alt="Beth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600268807p2/44125660.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1575587444?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth" href="/user/show/44125660-beth">Beth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44125660-beth?shelf=book-series">book-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44125660-beth?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44125660-beth?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1575587444" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10451056141378747945"><i>The Winner's Curse is when you come out on top of the bid, but only by paying a steep price.</i><br/><br/>Where do I even begin with this review? <b>This. I did not expect this.</b><br/><br/>Honestly, this was never ending, to say it's not the biggest book in the world SO much happens! There were parts where I was like how is this even happening?! The building of the storyline was so well done, and forever had me guessing what was coming next. Not only that, but we saw different difficulties coming in to play and how not ever</span>
  <span id="freeText10451056141378747945" style="display:none"><i>The Winner's Curse is when you come out on top of the bid, but only by paying a steep price.</i><br /><br />Where do I even begin with this review? <b>This. I did not expect this.</b><br /><br />Honestly, this was never ending, to say it's not the biggest book in the world SO much happens! There were parts where I was like how is this even happening?! The building of the storyline was so well done, and forever had me guessing what was coming next. Not only that, but we saw different difficulties coming in to play and how not everything can happen.<br /><br />My heart broke so many time for Kestrel and Arin, it's so hard to explain. I had <u>such</u> conflicting views about both of these characters, but overall I'm so happy with how they grew.<br /><br /><i>"In the dark. You... you look like an open flame" - Arin</i><br /><br />We have <b>Kestrel,</b> she admits she's not the best fighter but doesn't want to show this as a weakness. We do however see how intelligent she is! I love all of her strategic moves and how she thinks of the little things no one else would. I just enjoyed seeing a character be true to themselves and knowing what there strengths and weakness's are rather than be something that they're not. I'm really looking forward to seeing how she progresses in the next books!<br /><br /><i> "You might not think of me as your friend,but I think of you as mine." - Kestrel</i><br /><br />Now we have <b>Arin</b> out of everyone in this book, I honestly didn't know where he stood, he had me questioning things over and over again and that's what I think I liked so much about him. There are so many unanswered questions I want to know more!<br /><br /><i>"My soul is yours. You know that it is." - Arin</i><br /><br />What I <b>liked?</b><br />- The book was just effortless, it flowed so well, it was easy to read, the chapters were short and well paced, something was continuously happening, just what I like in a book!<br />- The world building for this was really interesting!<br />- I enjoy the whole "Star-Crossed Lovers" type thing. <i>(Yes I am rooting for them)</i><br /><br />What I <b>didn't like?</b><br />- How to word this... we got glimpses of side characters, but they literally meant nothing! I don't know how to explain this. I love that the focus is on Arin and Kestrel, I really do. <b>However</b> we didn't see a lot of other characters, a prime example of this is Cheat. I wanted to know so much more about his character, but really what did we know/find out about him?<br />- There are so many open ended questions, will we find out what they actually mean orrrrr?!<br /><br />Overall I honestly really enjoyed this book, if I didn't already have the second book I would be <i>weeping</i> at that ending, how can it leave us there wanting to find out what happens next?! Luckily for me I have the next book! <b>YAY!</b><br /><br /><i>She would bring the hounds of the empire howling down on this city</i><br /><br /><b>The Winner's Curse - 4 Stars</b><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1575587502?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1%20-%204%20Stars" rel="nofollow noopener">The Winner's Crime</a> - 4 Stars<br /><b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1575587516" rel="nofollow noopener">The Winner's Kiss</a> - 4 Stars</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="10451056141378747945" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2012882749" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2012882749" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2012882749?book_show_action=true">Dec 25, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2019">z-read2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2000">y-out2000</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-series">x-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=sff-high-fantasy">sff-high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2012882749" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12045147727629015824"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>People in brightly lit places cannot see into the dark.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>I guess we’re back on the bandwagon of reading 2010s-published YA fantasy that I missed out on when I was probably in the right age range to appreciate it. It is with gladness in my heart that I say I was very engaged with this fantasy, following a world inspired by Greco-Roman slavery and two main characters from different sides. It is with a heavier heart that I say some aspects of it really were not hitting their marks. <br/><br/>The be</span>
  <span id="freeText12045147727629015824" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>People in brightly lit places cannot see into the dark.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />I guess we’re back on the bandwagon of reading 2010s-published YA fantasy that I missed out on when I was probably in the right age range to appreciate it. It is with gladness in my heart that I say I was very engaged with this fantasy, following a world inspired by Greco-Roman slavery and two main characters from different sides. It is with a heavier heart that I say some aspects of it really were not hitting their marks. <br /><br />The best thing about this book is the entire idea behind Kestral’s character. Kestral is, possibly, the most non-archetypal strong female character I think I’ve seen in popular ya lit from this time period. Kestral is actively not a fighter and can’t hold a sword for shit. She is also, however, <b>an incredible manipulator.</b> She does it a lot. Successfully. At one point she does it to a terrible man she is fighting and it's by far the best scene in this book. I get very into mind games and it was this that held my attention the most. Were this book in a completely different setting and nothing but Kestral playing mind games I would have been obsessed and given it five stars do not @ me. <br /><br />Arin was a character I wanted to like so bad but his internal narration is just… deeply frustrating. I feel like when you have a main character who makes a lot of bad decisions, it needs to be justified with <i>strong</i> characterization. I felt like in comparison Kestrel was so much more complex, which is hilarious, because Arin is the character whose side I was rooting for way more in this. (He did grow on me over time.) And almost all of the side characters are instantly forgettable. Sorry, Ronan, the most transparent attempt at a good guy trope I’ve seen in years. <br /><br />The thing that I feel complex about is the issue of <b>slavery</b>. Let’s go through a few points. <br /><br />So, first off, slavery presents a power imbalance no matter what context it appears in. Having a romance between a master and a slave, no matter what the context, presents a huge power imbalance and arguably an automatically bad one. This is very clearly an allegory for Greco-Roman slavery, rather than chattel slavery, which are admittedly very different. (Were this an allegory for chattel slavery this romance would be genuinely disgusting do not pass go do not collect $500.) I think I feel similarly about this to how I feel about parts of <i>An Ember in the Ashes</i>: much as I know that no character plans to/ever threatens to violate boundaries, there’s <b>a power dynamic between the main couple that means they <i>could</i></b>, and that in and of itself makes certain scenes uncomfortable rather than romantic. <br /><br />The conflict between the Hermanii and the Valori is handled in a manner that is at times good and at times sort of a mess. I liked that the conquered nation was in-text the peaceful, art-loving one and the conquering nation the ‘barbaric’ one. A lot more accurate to actual histories! I appreciated that though Kestral herself is xenophobic, the book criticizes her views heavily over time. I wished this had happened before any of the romance had taken place, as I genuinely could not get invested in a romance essentially between a xenophobe and the person she’s xenophobic towards. (Since we've brought up <i>An Ember In the Ashes</i>, I could not help mentioning <i>that</i> book avoids this particular crime, which is a <i>huge</i> difference.)<br /><br />There are some redeeming qualities, however, specifically in the second half of the book. First of all: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[halfway through the book, the book flips on its head, and Kestral becomes the oppressed, with Arin as the member of a conquering nation <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. This was handled interestingly. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The idea of turning all of Kestral and Arin’s power plays on their head is a good one. However, the book then becomes far more sympathetic to the Valorian cause than I would’ve expected, given they literally conquered and enslaved an entire people. Not to be like colonists bad, but colonists bad. Also, the Herrani's motivations get mildly dubious, which I <i>thiiink</i> is the point? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The thing is, <b>we live in a very different context than the Greco-Roman period, with our own histories that make certain clearly not-badly-intentioned aspects of this book uncomfortable</b>. And due to all of those different factors, I really struggled to get invested in this romance. At this point I’m invested enough in both of these characters to care anyway, but we’ll have to see where this goes. <br /><br />My final note on this book is that I kind of love the ending. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I absolutely love the purposeful miscommunication to save someone’s life trope. I don’t know. I love it so much. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> And I have also heard <i>many</i> times that in comparison to the other books this book is not quite as good. So I don’t know. Maybe second book good. I’ll at least give it a shot. <br /><br />Amazing how this review took me four months to write. I'm on catchup mode. I promise someday soon I will no longer be on catchup mode. <br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/sockamommy" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookishactress/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://sptfy.com/4F6I" rel="nofollow noopener">Spotify</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/thebookishactress" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://thebookishactress.carrd.co/#about" rel="nofollow noopener">About</a> |</span>
  <a data-text-id="12045147727629015824" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1195286134" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1195286134" />
    <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson"><img alt="Whitney Atkinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550868411p2/14457130.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1195286134?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer4571371060784849662">So I finished this book a few days ago now, and can I just say, I don't <i>remember</i> the last time a book hit me so hard.   <span id="freeText4571371060784849662" style="display:none">So I finished this book a few days ago now, and can I just say, I don't <i>remember</i> the last time a book hit me so hard. This was a book I wanted to give my full attention to and couldn't wait to review. <br /><br />I'll try to grow this review into my trademark ranty sort soon, but for now, this will have to do.<br />IT'S ALL MY EMOTIONS WILL LET ME DO.<br /><br />So here we have it. <b>Reasons to Read <i>The Winner's Curse</i> Because Emotional Death is Fun:</b><br /><br />• The author's name is Marie. Clearly a name of legend *cough cough* so you know. She must be magical. Just like me. ✨ (Sparkles to prove my magicalness, obviously.)<br />• There's a PIANO PLAYING MAIN CHARACTER. Do you hear me roaring??? I wish we had more musical characters and HERE WE HAVE HER. She's also super cunning and strategic and kind to boot. Like I want to be this girl??<br />• We are blessed with a slowly developed romance and it made me all kinds of happy.<br />• THERE'S A SUPER FABULOUSLY WRITTEN ROMANESQUE WORLD THAT HONESTLY HAD SOME OF THE BEST WORLDBUILDING I'VE READ FOR A LONG WHILE &amp; IT MIGHT HAVE STOLEN MY BREATH AWAY ALONG WITH MY UNCAPITALIZED LETTERS. SO THERE'S THAT.<br />• This was also a book that made me stop what I was doing and read for hours on end. I don't remember the last time a book has soaked up my attention so completely and I could hardly bear to put the book down. Unless it was to stare at it.<br />Because I mean WHO WOULDN'T IT'S STINKING GORGEOUS.<br />• I actually cared about the characters. Like they're my family. Don't mess with them or I WILL THROW MY BOOKS AT YOU AND POTENTIALLY MAIM YOU. You have been warned.<br />• I'm obsessed. It's official.<br /><br />Please let me know if that list wasn't good enough. I'd be happy to scream more reasons at you in the comments.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2368556254" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2368556254" />
    <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz"><img alt="Helena of Eretz ✰" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596076376p2/27036454.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2368556254?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helena of Eretz ✰" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz">Helena of Eretz ✰</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780374384678" href="/book/show/17756559-the-winner-s-curse">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=hardback">hardback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=greco-roman">greco-roman</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2368556254" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4437207783091662877"><i>“The Winner’s Curse is when you come out on top of the bid, but only by paying a steep price.”</i> <br/><br/>Ok, so I don’t know what happened to this buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1593618210' rel='nofollow noopener'>Laura</a>, but I’m just going to go ahead with this review as it’s been sitting here in RTC-mode since 19 August. :D It’s about time, guys and gals!<br/><br/>All right! So, I was <b>ecstatic</b> about this book, after completing it, (as I read it in nearly one sitting initially) because I found the writing style to be <i>so engaging</i> and the plot to be <i>so addicting</i>. How</span>
  <span id="freeText4437207783091662877" style="display:none"><i>“The Winner’s Curse is when you come out on top of the bid, but only by paying a steep price.”</i> <br /><br />Ok, so I don’t know what happened to this buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1593618210" rel="nofollow noopener">Laura</a>, but I’m just going to go ahead with this review as it’s been sitting here in RTC-mode since 19 August. :D It’s about time, guys and gals!<br /><br />All right! So, I was <b>ecstatic</b> about this book, after completing it, (as I read it in nearly one sitting initially) because I found the writing style to be <i>so engaging</i> and the plot to be <i>so addicting</i>. However, as more and more time passed since I read this, I found <b>more and more problems</b> with this novel, which is quite unfortunate, considering what a beloved trilogy this is among the YA community (or so I’ve been told, anyway). <br /><br />My first issue is that for a trilogy marketed as high fantasy…literally everywhere I looked…<i>WHERE WAS THE FANTASY?!</i> If anything, it’s like an alternate-history timeline. To me, it read like an Ancient Roman-based society, with post-Edwardian era clothing (think Downton Abbey). If I’m being completely honest though, aside from the <b>false advertising</b>, the lack of fantasy didn’t bother me <i>that much</i>, once I got into the story. I just think that it would be more apropos to consider this as <b>historical fiction</b>, rather than fantasy. Also, there were quite a few <i>dystopian aspects</i> included, as well (which aren’t really my thing, but whatevs). Essentially, this novel is more of a <b>romance</b>, rather than anything else. I don’t know about you, but I was hoping for more cutthroat characters and bloody scenes (like Ancient Rome historically was), but this book was <i>pretty tame</i>, in all actuality. <br /><br />The “<i>world-building</i>,” per se, was virtually <b>non-existent</b>. Literally all we learn about this world is that the society is divided between the <b>Valorians</b> and the <b>Herrani</b>. The Valorians stress importance on <i>militant values</i>, whereas the Herrani prefer <i>artistic</i> ones. The Valorians are the <b>conquerors</b> and the Herrani are the now-conquered <b>slaves</b>. And that’s literally <i>it</i>. I mean, come onnnnn… Despite that, I was fascinated by the mentions of the <i>war history</i> in this world, and even specific battles. However, these were rather far and few between, and I hope that they shall be fleshed out in the future instalments of this trilogy. I’ve heard that this series seriously improves as it goes on, which has me very hopeful! ;)<br /><br /><i>“Kestrel's cruel calculation appalled her. This was part of what had made her resist the military: the fact that she could make decisions like this, that she did have a mind for strategy, that people could be so easily become pieces in a game she was determined to win...”</i><br /><br />On a more positive note, I did find <b>Kestrel</b> to be <i>the highlight</i> of this novel! She was brilliant! Too often, female protagonists are only considered as “strong female characters” if they are physically strong, like the <i>oh-so-popular</i> Celaena Sardothien (from Throne of Glass). It was refreshing to come across a protagonist who was <b>mentally strong</b> and physically weak, but <i>OWNS IT</i> unashamedly. Even when in a duel, Kestrel manages to outwit her opponent, rather than besting them with a blade. Finally, we have a character that I can relate to! :D (I like to think that I’m mentally fit anyway, hahaha)<br /><br />If you know my bookish tastes at all, you could probably guess that the one aspect of the novel that I hated the <i>most</i> was the <b>slavery trope</b>. Can this literary trope just die already? I’m sick of seeing it everywhere. Don’t get me wrong…I’ve read a few New Adult dark romances that provide a discourse on the psychology behind the Master/Slave dynamic and Stockholm Syndrome, but this book used slavery as a <b>plot device</b>, which I wasn’t a fan of. Let’s begin with the fact that Arin didn’t even act like a bloody slave, in the first place! He did what he wanted <i>when</i> he wanted and talked back to his “master” (Kestrel) at every opportunity. He was so <b>unbelievable</b> in the role that he portrayed. How anyone could take him seriously was beyond me! Also, Kestrel was a <b>laughable</b> as a slave-owner, seeing as she permitted Arin to do as he pleased. I’m so confused over their dynamic and how they could have possibly fallen in love with each other (they didn’t even spend that much time with each other). Let’s also take into account that while Kestrel freed <i>one slave</i> in the past, she never explicitly states the inherent <b>wrongness</b> of the purchasing and selling of other human beings. Come on, Kestrel! I know that you’re better than that! In addition, you <i>never connect</i> with the slaves themselves. You hear that they are oppressed and that their culture was destroyed, but we never see any of the brutality directed at the slaves. We are told that they are scarred, but we aren’t shown their daily treatment, which makes it impossible for the reader to commiserate with their plight. I wanted to care…but I just didn’t (nor couldn’t). <br /><br />Despite this book’s many faults, I am still <i>looking forward</i> to the second and third instalments in this trilogy. While I’m not a fan of the world-building or the romance, I <i>am</i> a fan of Kestrel, and can’t wait to see what the future holds for her. This was a <b>strong introduction</b> to this world, and I enjoyed it quite a bit! :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="4437207783091662877" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2708149608" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14511071016380148021">It’s a 4.5 star rating for the book by itself, but the narrator was no for me. It was killing me listening to the book and it was painful because I liked this story a lot and a friend of mine is reading for the first time and so I got nostalgic… it was a bummer. I did not enjoy it whatsoever and maybe it was me who didn’t click with the narrator but it was painful nonetheless. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('YSNSES3nR9V5nUwO3DAAOUUWK9j4B1I9gkeY9iWaDvhkwpCc3Uh2qHmzx9vXIx33i0g5J32fMJjCw5ksV+vY/A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZXgb+eMw9D1MayFx8Ed8BOQsd7HmvI6HK/ammxA9Jihgmdl0E5/FQExFqqT7VGHKKnJlTmMk7CJrcqdBYkzwLA==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6995139616908439517">Marie Rutkoski is the <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author of The Winner's Trilogy, which begins with <i>The Winner's Curse</i>. She also wrote the YA novel <i>The Shadow Society</i> and the children's fantasy series The Kronos Chronicles, including <i>The Cabinet of Wonders</i>. Her next project is a YA duology set in the same world as <i>The Winner's Curse</i>. The first in this duology is called <i>The Midnight Lie</i> and will be </span>
  <span id="freeText6995139616908439517" style="display:none">Marie Rutkoski is the <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author of The Winner's Trilogy, which begins with <i>The Winner's Curse</i>. She also wrote the YA novel <i>The Shadow Society</i> and the children's fantasy series The Kronos Chronicles, including <i>The Cabinet of Wonders</i>. Her next project is a YA duology set in the same world as <i>The Winner's Curse</i>. The first in this duology is called <i>The Midnight Lie</i> and will be published in March 2020. <br /><br />Marie grew up in Bolingbrook, Illinois (a suburb of Chicago), as the oldest of four children. She holds a BA from the University of Iowa and a PhD from Harvard University. Marie is currently a professor at Brooklyn College, where she teaches Renaissance Drama, children's literature and fiction writing. She lives in Brooklyn with her two sons.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://us.macmillan.com/author/marierutkoski">http://us.macmillan.com/author/marier...</a></span>

This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
